Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
The Deputy's Authority to Marry Minors: Condition in the Patent and Related Rulings
Condition for the deputy's authority to marry minors and the ruling on marrying the deputy's own son.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the condition required for a deputy (na'ib) to have authority to marry minors and evaluate the validity of such marriages, including the case of marrying the deputy's own son.

Core Idea
A deputy only has authority to marry minors if explicitly granted in his patent; general delegation does not include marriage.

The authority of a qadi's deputy (na'ib) to marry minors is not automatic. It hinges on the wording of his appointment patent (manshur). Furthermore, whether the deputy can marry a minor to his own son involves a qiyas between an agent and a judge. This lesson dissects these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the chain of authority
The sultan delegates to the qadi, who may delegate to a deputy. The deputy's authority derives from the qadi.
2
Identify the condition in the patent
The deputy's patent must explicitly include the authority to marry minors (tazwij al-sighar).
Without this condition, the deputy has no such authority.
3
Distinguish between general and specific delegation
General delegation of 'judgment' does not include marriage; marriage requires explicit mention.
This is based on the text: 'if they are conditionally granted in their patent the marriage of minors, otherwise not.'
4
Analyze the sub-issue: marrying the deputy's own son
The deputy marrying a minor to his own son is analogous to an agent (permissible) but also analogous to a judge (prohibited). The relied-upon view deems it void.
The text states: 'if the qadi married the small girl to his son, it is void.'
5
Conclude with the mufta bihi
The deputy lacks authority without the condition; even with authority, marriage to his son is invalid.
The reasoning: it is a judgment for himself, which is not allowed.

قال : والإلحاق بالوكيل يكفي للحكم مستغن عن جعل فعله حكماً مع انتفاء شرطه ا هـ . وفي الفوائد الناجية معزياً إلى فتاوى سمرقند : سئل القاضي بديع الدين عن صغيرة زوجت نفسها ولا ولي لها ولا قاضي في ذلك الموضع قال : يتوقف وينفذ بإجازتها بعد بلوغها ا هـ . مع أنهم قالوا : كل عقد لا يجيز له حال صدوره فهو باطل لا يتوقف، ولعل التوقف فيه باعتبار أن مجيزه السلطان كما لا يخفى. وفي النوازل والذخيرة امرأة جاءت إلى قاض فقالت له أريد أن أتزوج ولا ولي لي فللقاضي أن يأذن لها في النكاح كما لو علم أن لها ولياً. وما نقل فيه من إقامتها البينة خلاف المشهور وما نقل من قول إسماعيل بن حماد بن أبي حنيفة يقول لها القاضي إن لم تكوني قرشية ولا عربية ولا ذات بعل ولا معتدة فقد أذنت لك، فالظاهر أن الشرطين الأولين محمولان على رواية عدم الجواز من غير الكفء، وأما الشرط الثالث فمعلوم الاشتراط. كذا في فتح القدير. والظاهر أن الشرطين الأولين إنما هو عند كذبها بأن كان لها ولي أما إن كانت صادقة في عدم الولي فليسا بشرطين على جميع الروايات. وأشار المصنف إلى أن وصي الصغير والصغيرة إذا لم يكن قريباً ولا حاكماً فإنه ليس له ولاية التزويج ، سواء كان أوصى إليه الأب في ذلك أو لم يوص. وروى هشام عن أبي حنيفة إن أوصى إليه الأب جاز له كذا في الخانية والظهيرية وبه علم أن ما في التبيين من أنه ليس له ذلك إلا أن يفوض إليه الموصي ذلك رواية هشام وهي ضعيفة، واستثنى في فتح القدير ما إذا كان الموصي عين رجلاً في حياته للتزويج فيزوجها الوصي كما لو وكل في حياته بتزويجها ا.هـ. وفيه نظر لأنه إن زوجها من المعين قبل موت الموصي فليس الكلام فيه

منشور قاضي القضاة فإن كان ذلك في عهد نائبه منه ملكه النائب وإلا فلا ولم أر فيه منقولاً صريحاً. وفي الظهيرية فإن زوجها القاضي ولم يأذن له أذن له بذلك فأجاز القاضي ذلك جاز استحساناً، وفي غاية البيان: ولو زوج القاضي الصغيرة من ابنه كان باطلاً. وكذا إذا باع مال اليتيم من نفسه لا يجوز لأنه حكم وحكمه لنفسه لا يجوز، ولو اشترى من وصي اليتيم يجوز وإن كان القاضي أقامه وصياً لأنه نائب عن الميت لا عن القاضي ا هـ . وعلله في فتح القدير بأنه كالوكيل لا يجوز عقده لابنه تفويض الأصيل للنائب كما توهمه في البحر ا هـ . قال الرملي أقول : كيف لا يفيد مع إطلاقه في نوابه والمطلق يجري على إطلاقه ووجهه أنه لما فوض لهم ماله ولايته التي من جملتها تزويج الصغار والصغائر صار ذلك من جملة ما فوض إليهم، وقد تقرر أنهم نواب السلطان حيث أذن له بالاستنابة عنه فيما فوضه إليه. وقد قال في الخلاصة والبزازية : ولا ولاية للقاضي إلا إذا كان ولياً قريباً ا هـ . وهو محمول على ما إذا كان في عهده ومنشوره وأقول : حيث قلنا بأنه ولي لوجود ذلك يدخل في المجيز الذي يتوقف نكاح الفضولي على إجازته حيث لا ولي غيره وهي واقعة الفتوى تأمل ا هـ . قلت : وقد ذكر المسألة الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل حيث قال : الظاهر أن النائب الذي لم ينص له القاضي على تزويج الصغار لا يملكه لأنه إن كان فوض إليه الحكم بين الناس فهذا مخصوص بالمرافعات، وإن قال استنبتك في الحكم فكذلك لا يتعدى إلى التزويج. أما لو قال له استنبتك في جميع ما فوض إلى السلطان فيملك لأنه استنابه في التزويج أيضاً حيث عمم له الولاية، ثم قال الطرسوسي : وهل يقال إنه إذا ملك التزويج في هذه الصورة هل له أن يأذن لأحد في التزويج أم لا؟ ليس له ذلك لأن ولايته في المعنى من السلطان وهو لم يأذن له في ذلك فلم يملكه فبقي كأحد العقاد المأذون لهم من الحاكم الأصل لأنه استفاد التزويج من جهة القاضي لا السلطان، ولأنه من بمنزلة الوكيل عن القاضي وليس للوكيل أن يوكل إلا بإذن . وهل يكون تزويجه هذا بمنزلة تزويجه إذا كانت الولاية له ويكون حكماً أم لا؟ وكذا هل يملك ذلك لابنه ولمن لا يجوز قضاؤه له أم لا؟ الظاهر أنه لا يكون حكماً ويملك مباشرته لابنه ونحوه. ولقائل أن هذا يمنع ويسوي بين الأول من حيث إن القاضي ولي أبعد فإذا أذن له الأقرب باشر بأهليته وبولايته بخلاف غيره من الناس إذا باشر بوكالة من الولي لأنه لا ولاية له أصلاً فهو وكيل محض . ا هـ ملخصاً قوله: (وعلله في فتح القدير) قال في النهر أقول : الإلحاق بالوكيل يقتضي أنه لو زوّج أو باع من ابنه أكثر من القيمة ومن مهر المثل جاز إذ لا خلاف في جواز بيع الوكيل ممن لا تقبل شهادته له بذلك، وتعليلهم بأن فعله حكم يقتضي المنع مطلقاً وهو الظاهر. وأيضاً الوكيل يلحقه العهدة والقاضي لا عهدة عليه وقد نص محمد في الأصل أن الورثة لو طلبوا القسمة وفيهم غائب أو وبين
Book of Marriage / Section on Competence (Kafa'ah). 221. He said: And analogy to the agent suffices for the ruling, independent of making his action a ruling while its condition is absent. End. In al-Fawa'id al-Najiyya, quoting from Fatawa Samarqand: Qadi Badi' al-Din was asked about a minor girl who married herself, having no guardian and no qadi in that place. He said: It is suspended and executed by her ratification after she reaches puberty. End. While they said: Every contract that has no ratifier at the time of its issuance is void, not suspended. Perhaps the suspension here is because its ratifier is the sultan, as is not hidden. In al-Nawazil and al-Dhakhira: A woman came to a qadi and said: I want to marry and I have no guardian. The qadi may permit her to marry, as if he knew she had a guardian. What is narrated about establishing her evidence is contrary to the well-known. And what is narrated from the saying of Isma'il ibn Hammad ibn Abi Hanifa: The qadi says to her: 'If you are not Qurayshi, nor Arab, nor a married woman, nor in 'idda, then I have permitted you.' So apparently the first two conditions are based on the narration of impermissibility from someone who is not a match (kuf'). As for the third condition, its requirement is known. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. And the apparent view is that the first two conditions are only when she is lying, i.e., she has a guardian; but if she is truthful in having no guardian, they are not conditions according to all narrations. The author indicated that the executor (wasi) of a minor boy or girl, if he is not a relative nor a ruler, has no guardianship of marriage, whether the father appointed him for that or not. Hisham narrated from Abu Hanifa: If the father appointed him, it is permissible. Thus in al-Khaniyya and al-Zahiriyya. Accordingly, what is in al-Tabyin that he does not have that unless the testator delegates it to him is the narration of Hisham, and it is weak. Fath al-Qadir made an exception: if the testator designated a specific person during his lifetime for marriage, then the executor marries her, just as if he appointed an agent during his lifetime for her marriage. End. There is consideration in this because if he married her to the designated person before the death of the testator, the discussion is not about that... between them. And I do not judge against the heir and the minor because the qadi's division is a judgment from him. Since the Imam has text on that, there is no room for investigation. If you say: What do you do with what they have agreed upon, that from the conditions of the enforceability of judgment in matters of ijtihad is that the judgment becomes an incident involving a valid complaint before the qadi from one opponent against another? I say: The apparent view is that it is applied to verbal judgment; as for actual judgment, that condition is not required, reconciling between their statements. His saying: 'Because its ratifier is the sultan' — meaning the qadi who is given authority to marry minors, because he is his deputy. Al-Ramli said: In it, that the premise of the case is where there is no qadi — ponder. I say: It should be restricted to not being in the abode of war. And it is objected by the case of a small girl who married with no guardian; its implication is suspension because she has a ratifier, the sultan. Then I saw a quotation from al-Ghaya at the statement of al-Hidaya: 'Every contract issued by a fuduli and it has a ratifier becomes suspended.' It is only restricted by 'and it has a ratifier' because if it does not, as when the fuduli marries an orphan, the contract is not suspended. It cannot be said that the sultan or qadi is a ratifier, so it should be suspended, because we say: The case can be assumed in a place with no qadi, like the abode of war. End. Ponder his saying: 'And the apparent view that the first two conditions, etc.' Al-Nahr said: This is unnecessary because the application cannot occur except on the assumption of her lying, since the disagreement is only when there is a guardian, not when there is none. As... and Allah is the Guide. His saying: 'There is consideration because if he married her, etc.' Al-Nahr said: And I say in al-Dhakhira: He has no guardianship in marriage. 220. The sultan. Then. Book of Marriage, Chapter on Guardians and Competent Matches. His patent that: Then the sultan, then the qadi, and his deputies if they are conditionally granted in their patent the marriage of minors, otherwise not. End. Based on this, the condition is only regarding the qadi, not his deputies. It is possible that it is a condition for both. So if it is written in the patent of the chief qadi, then if that is in the deputy's charter from him, the deputy owns it; otherwise not. I have not seen a clear transmitted text on that. In al-Zahiriyya: If the qadi married her and he (the deputy) did not have permission, then the qadi ratified it, it is permissible by istihsan. In Ghayat al-Bayan: If the qadi married the small girl to his son, it is void. Similarly, if he sold the property of the orphan to himself, it is not permissible because it is a judgment, and his judgment for himself is not permissible. If he bought from the executor of the orphan, it is permissible, even if the qadi appointed him as executor, because he is a deputy of the deceased, not of the qadi. End. He gave the cause in Fath al-Qadir: It is like the agent; he may not contract for his son, delegating the principal to the deputy, as was imagined in al-Bahr. End. Al-Ramli said: I say: How does it not benefit with its absoluteness regarding his deputies? The absolute runs on its absoluteness. The reason is that when he delegated to them what he has authority over, which includes marrying minors, that became part of what he delegated to them. It has been established that they are deputies of the sultan if he permitted him to delegate on his behalf in what he delegated to him. It is stated in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyya: The qadi has no authority unless he is a close relative. End. It is applied to the case when it is in his patent and charter. And I say: Since we say he is a guardian due to that, he enters into the category of ratifier on whose ratification the marriage of the fuduli is suspended, when there is no other guardian, and this is the fatwa case — ponder. End. I say: Al-Tarsusi mentioned the case in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, where he said: The apparent view is that the deputy who is not explicitly given authority by the qadi to marry minors does not possess it, because if he delegated to him judgment among the people, that is specific to litigation; if he said 'I appoint you as deputy in judgment,' similarly it does not extend to marriage. But if he said to him 'I appoint you as deputy in everything delegated to the sultan,' then he possesses it because he appointed him as deputy in marriage as well, by generalizing authority. Then al-Tarsusi said: Is it said that when he possesses marriage in this form, does he have the right to permit someone else to marry or not? He does not have that, because his authority in meaning is from the sultan, and he did not permit him to that, so he does not possess it; thus he remains like one of the ordinary contractors permitted by the original ruler, because he derived marriage from the qadi, not the sultan; and because he is like an agent of the qadi, and an agent may not delegate another except with permission. And is his marriage like his marriage when he has authority, and is it a judgment or not? Similarly, does he possess it for his son and for those for whom his judgment is not permissible or not? The apparent view is that it is not a judgment, and he may perform it for his son and the like. One could argue that this prevents and equates with the first, in that the qadi is a remote guardian, so when the closer one permits him, he acts by his own capacity and authority, unlike other people who act with agency from the guardian because they have no authority at all; they are pure agents. End, summarized. His saying: 'He gave the cause in Fath al-Qadir.' Al-Nahr said: I say: The analogy to the agent implies that if he married or sold from his son for more than the value and more than the proper dower, it is permissible, since there is no disagreement about the permissibility of the agent selling to someone whose testimony is not acceptable for him. Their reasoning that his action is a judgment implies prohibition absolutely, and that is the apparent view. Also, the agent is liable, while the qadi is not liable. Muhammad stated in al-Asl: If the heirs request division and among them is an absent or minor, the Imam said: I do not divide... and between.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary (sharh) from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the section of Kafa'ah (competence) from Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The text examines the authority of various persons to conclude the marriage contract for minors, a critical issue in Hanafi nikah. It begins by discussing a case from Fatawa Samarqand: a minor girl marries herself without a guardian or qadi. The ruling is that the contract is suspended (mawquf) and becomes valid upon her ratification after puberty. The commentator notes that normally a contract without a ratifier at inception is batil (void), but here the suspension is allowed because the sultan (or qadi) is a potential ratifier. The passage then addresses the scenario of a woman who claims to have no guardian; the qadi may permit her to marry if she meets certain conditions (not Qurayshi, not Arab, not married, not in 'idda). These conditions are explained as being for cases where she may be lying about having a guardian; if she is truthful, no such conditions apply. The text then turns to the authority of the wasi (executor). The author of Kanz indicates that a wasi who is neither a relative nor a ruler has no guardianship to marry minors, even if the father appointed him for that. A weak narration from Hisham permits it if the father appointed him, but the relied-upon view is that it is not allowed unless the testator specifically designated a person for marriage during his lifetime, in which case the wasi may carry out that marriage. The commentator notes a contradiction: if the designated person was already the husband, then the marriage would have occurred before death, so the discussion is moot. The text then moves to the authority of the qadi's deputy (na'ib). The key principle from al-Hidaya is that a contract by a fuduli (unauthorized person) is suspended only if it has a ratifier. For a minor orphan without a guardian, the sultan or qadi can be the ratifier. However, if there is no qadi (e.g., in dar al-harb), the contract is not suspended. The deputy's authority to marry minors depends on the wording of his appointment. If the patent (manshur) from the chief qadi includes explicit authorization to marry minors, the deputy has that authority; otherwise, he does not. Some authorities (e.g., al-Tarsusi) argue that the deputy, even if generally authorized, cannot sub-delegate because he acts as an agent of the qadi, not the sultan. The passage also discusses whether the deputy's marriage for his own son is valid; the analogy to a wakil (agent) suggests it would be permissible, but if the qadi's action is considered a judgment (hukm), it would be prohibited because a judge cannot judge for himself. The commentator favors the latter view. Overall, the passage demonstrates the Hanafi method of resolving disputes between different narrations and analogies, ultimately preferring the view that restricts authority to marry minors to specific, clearly delegated individuals.

Key Terms
نائب (na'ib): Deputy of a qadi; a person appointed by the qadi to exercise judicial or administrative functions on his behalf.
مجيز (mujiz): Ratifier; the person who has the authority to approve a contract that was concluded without proper authorization (e.g., by a fuduli).
منشور (manshur): Patent or official charter of appointment for a qadi or deputy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is required for a deputy (na'ib) of the qadi to have authority to marry a minor?
A) The deputy must be a close relative of the minor.
B) The deputy must have been explicitly authorized to marry minors in his patent (manshur).
C) The deputy automatically has this authority as part of his general delegation.
D) The deputy must seek permission from the sultan each time.

Key Takeaway
A deputy (na'ib) can marry minors only if his patent explicitly grants that authority; even then, marriage to his own son is void.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Authority of the Judge's Deputy to Marry Minors
Clarifies the conditions for a judge's deputy to marry minors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a judge's deputy may validly contract marriage for minors and identify the effect of explicit authorization.

Core Idea
The deputy's authority to marry minors depends solely on explicit stipulation in the appointment charter.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the scope of a judge's deputy's authority regarding marriage of minors. The Hanafi school requires that such authority be explicitly granted in the judge's charter. Without it, the deputy acts without power, though the judge may later validate the marriage by istihsan. We will examine the conditions, the evidence, and the intra-school differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act in question is a deputy judge (na'ib) contracting marriage for a minor (saghir/saghira). The ruling is that such a marriage is valid only if the deputy's charter (manshur) explicitly includes the authority to marry minors. If not, the marriage is invalid unless the judge subsequently ratifies it.
2
Locate the condition for validity
The key condition for the deputy's authority is explicit mention (shart) in the appointment charter. The authors debate whether the condition applies only to the judge or also to his deputies. The majority view is that it applies to both, but the deputy must be explicitly named.
The text references the 'ahd wa manshur (charter) as the source of authority.
3
Trace the dalil (proof)
The main proofs are istihsan (juristic preference) and analogy (qiyas) to agency (wakalah). Istihsan allows the judge to validate a marriage performed without authority. Qiyas treats the deputy like an agent who cannot act beyond his mandate.
The dalil_block in the toolbox identifies the use of istihsan and qiyas.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a difference within the Hanafi school: some scholars hold that the condition for authority (stipulation in the charter) applies only to the judge, not automatically to his deputy. Others, including the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, argue that the condition must be read into the deputy's authority as well.
This difference affects whether a general appointment gives marriage powers.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative position)
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that the deputy does NOT have authority to marry minors unless the charter explicitly grants it. This is the safer view and aligns with the principle that authority must be expressly delegated.
The author inclines toward this view, citing al-Tarsusi.

Source Text

ثم السلطان ثم القاضي ونوّابه إذا اشترط في عهده تزويج الصغار والصغائر وإلا فلا ا هـ . بناء على هذا الشرط إنما هو في حق القاضي دون نوابه، ويحتمل أن يكون شرطاً فيهما ، فإذا كتب في منشور قاضي القضاة فإن جملتها تزويج الصغار والصغائر صار ذلك من جملة ما فوض إليهم، وقد تقرر أنهم نواب السلطان حيث أذن له بالاستنابة عنه فيما فوضه إليه. وقد قال في الخلاصة والبزازية : ولا ولاية للقاضي إلا إذا كان ولياً قريباً الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل حيث قال : الظاهر أن النائب الذي لم ينص له القاضي على تزويج الصغار لا يملكه لأنه إن كان فوض إليه الحكم بين الناس فهذا مخصوص بالمرافعات، وإن قال استنبتك في الحكم فكذلك لا يتعدى إلى التزويج. أما لو قال له استنبتك في جميع ما فوض إلى السلطان فيملك لأنه استنابه في التزويج أيضاً حيث عمم له الولاية، ثم قال الطرسوسي : وهل يقال إنه إذا ملك التزويج في هذه الصورة هل له أن يأذن لأحد في التزويج أم لا؟ ليس له ذلك لأن ولايته في المعنى من السلطان وهو لم يأذن له في ذلك فلم يملكه فبقي كأحد العقاد المأذون لهم من الحاكم الأصل لأنه استفاد التزويج من جهة القاضي لا السلطان، ولأنه من بمنزلة الوكيل عن القاضي وليس للوكيل أن يوكل إلا بإذن . وهل يكون تزويجه هذا بمنزلة تزويجه إذا كانت الولاية له ويكون حكماً أم لا؟ وكذا هل يملك ذلك لابنه ولمن لا يجوز قضاؤه له أم لا؟ الظاهر أنه لا يكون حكماً ويملك مباشرته لابنه ونحوه. ولقائل أن هذا يمنع ويسوي بين الأول من حيث إن القاضي ولي أبعد فإذا أذن له الأقرب باشر بأهليته وبولايته بخلاف غيره من الناس إذا باشر بوكالة من الولي لأنه لا ولاية له أصلاً فهو وكيل محض . ا هـ ملخصاً قوله: (وعلله في فتح القدير) قال في النهر أقول : الإلحاق بالوكيل يقتضي أنه لو زوّج أو باع من ابنه أكثر من القيمة ومن مهر المثل جاز إذ لا خلاف في جواز بيع الوكيل ممن لا تقبل شهادته له بذلك، وتعليلهم بأن فعله حكم يقتضي المنع مطلقاً وهو الظاهر. وأيضاً الوكيل يلحقه العهدة والقاضي لا عهدة عليه وقد نص محمد في الأصل أن الورثة لو طلبوا القسمة وفيهم غائب أو صغير قال الإمام: لا أقسم وبين
Then the sultan, then the judge and his deputies if [marrying minors] is stipulated in his charter; otherwise not. Based on this, the condition is only for the judge, not his deputies, but it is possible it is a condition for both. So if it is written in the charter of the chief judge, then if that was in the deputy's charter, he is authorized; otherwise not. I have not seen an explicit transmitted text on this. In al-Zahiriyyah: If the judge marries her [the minor] and the deputy had not been permitted but then the judge gives permission and validates it, that is valid by istihsan. In Ghayat al-Bayan: If the judge marries a minor girl to his son, it is void. Similarly, if he sells the orphan's property to himself, it is not permitted because it is a judgment, and his judgment for himself is not valid. If he buys from the orphan's executor, it is valid even if the judge appointed him as executor because he is a deputy of the deceased, not of the judge. And he gave the reason in Fath al-Qadir that he is like an agent (wakil); his contract for his son is not valid, contrary to what was imagined in al-Bahr. Al-Ramli said: How is it not useful with his general wording regarding his deputies? The general applies as general, and the proof is that when he delegated to them his authority which includes marrying minors, that became part of what he delegated. And it has been established that they are deputies of the sultan if he permitted him to delegate. And it was said in al-Khulasa and al-Bazzaziyyah: The judge has no authority unless he is a close relative. This is interpreted as when it is in his charter. And I say: Where we say he is a guardian due to that, he enters into the category of the one whose permission is necessary for the marriage of a fuduli to be valid where there is no other guardian. This is the issue of fatwa, reflect. I say: Al-Tarsusi mentioned this issue in Anfa' al-Wasa'il, saying: The apparent view is that the deputy who was not explicitly instructed by the judge to marry minors does not have the authority, because if he delegated to him judgment among people, that is specific to litigation. If he said 'I appoint you as my deputy in judgment,' that also does not extend to marriage. But if he said 'I appoint you as my deputy in all that has been delegated to the sultan,' then he does have the authority because he delegated marriage as well by generalizing the authority. Then al-Tarsusi said: If he has the authority to marry in this case, can he delegate it to someone else? No, because his authority is essentially from the sultan, and he did not permit him to delegate, so he does not own it, remaining like one of the contractors authorized by the original ruler because he derived marriage authority from the judge, not the sultan, and he is like an agent of the judge, and an agent cannot delegate except with permission. And is his marriage considered as a judgment (hukm) or not? Similarly, does he have the authority to marry his own son or those for whom he cannot judge? The apparent view is that it is not a judgment, and he may directly perform it for his son and the like. One might say this is prevented and equated with the first because the judge is a distant guardian, and if the closer guardian gives permission, he acts with his own capacity and authority, unlike others who act as agents of the guardian because they have no authority at all; they are pure agents. Summarized. His statement: (And he gave the reason in Fath al-Qadir). He said in al-Nahr: I say: The analogy with the agent implies that if he married or sold to his son for more than market value or more than the proper dower, it would be valid, as there is no disagreement about the validity of a sale by an agent to someone whose testimony is not accepted for him. Their reasoning that his action is a judgment requires absolute prohibition, and that is apparent. Also, the agent bears liability (uhda), while the judge does not. Muhammad stated in al-Asl: If the heirs request division and among them is an absent person or a minor, the Imam said: I will not divide.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses the authority of a judge's deputy (na'ib) to contract marriages for minors (sighar). The author explains that the judge only has this authority if it is stipulated in his appointment charter (manshur). Regarding the deputy, there is a difference: some say the condition only applies to the judge not his deputies, while others say it applies to both. The author notes he found no explicit transmitted text on this point. The text then cites al-Zahiriyyah: if a judge marries a minor without permission from the deputy, but later validates it, it is valid by istihsan. However, in Ghayat al-Bayan, if the judge marries a minor to his own son, it is void, because a judge cannot pass a judgment for his own benefit. Similarly, selling orphan's property to himself is invalid. Buying from the orphan's executor is valid because the executor is a deputy of the deceased, not of the judge. In Fath al-Qadir, this is analogized to an agent (wakil) who cannot contract for his own son. Al-Ramli objects, arguing that the general wording of the charter should include the deputy, but it is concluded that the deputy only has authority if it is explicitly granted. The text then cites al-Tarsusi's detailed analysis: if the judge says 'I appoint you in judgment,' that does not include marriage; only if he says 'in all that the sultan has delegated' does it include marriage. The deputy himself cannot delegate this authority to another. The discussion ends with a comparison between the deputy acting as a judgment (hukm) or as a pure agent.

Key Terms
نائب القاضي (na'ib al-qadi): A deputy appointed by the judge to perform certain judicial functions, including marriage of minors if authorized.
عهد ومنشور ('ahd wa manshur): The appointment charter issued by the sultan or chief judge specifying the judge's authority.
الفضولي (al-fuduli): A person who acts without permission, whose contract requires subsequent approval.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what condition is necessary for a judge's deputy to have authority to marry minors?
A) The deputy must be a close relative of the minor.
B) The judge must be absent.
C) The authority must be explicitly stipulated in the appointment charter (manshur).
D) The deputy must be a Hanafi scholar.

Key Takeaway
Deputy cannot marry minors unless the appointment charter explicitly grants that authority; without it, the marriage is invalid unless the judge later validates it.

Order of Guardians in Marriage: Mother, Grandmother, Sister
Establishes the hierarchy of female marriage guardians after the father.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the complete order of marriage guardians (awliya') after the father according to the Hanafi school, identify the prevailing position on the mother-sister dispute, and explain the ruling for the defective grandfather.

Core Idea
The mother precedes the sister in marriage guardianship because proximity outweighs paternal lineage.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi hierarchy of marriage guardians after the father. The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lists the order and addresses a key dispute: whether the mother or the full sister has greater right. The relied-upon position prioritizes the mother. We also learn about the defective grandfather and the role of non-agnatic relatives (dhawu al-arham). This hierarchy is essential knowledge for anyone studying Hanafi marriage law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the immediate successors
After the father, the mother is the first guardian. Then list the daughters in descending order: daughter, son's daughter, son's son's daughter, daughter's daughter's daughter.
2
Recognize the dispute
Some early Hanafis (Khwahar Zadeh, Umar al-Nasafi) held the full sister is more entitled than the mother. Understand their basis (paternal lineage) and the counter-argument (proximity). The mufta bihi is mother first.
Refer to al-Khulasa and Fath al-Qadir.
3
Learn the position on the defective grandfather
Abu Hanifa places the defective grandfather after the mother but before the sister. Abu Yusuf equates them. The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.
4
Understand the inclusion of non-agnates
The passage covers asabat and dhawu al-arham, with the master of emancipation (mawla al-'itaqa) and his asabat taking precedence over the mother. Also note that the father's mother (grandmother) outranks the mother.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بعد الأم البنت ثم بنت الابن ثم بنت ابن الابن ثم بنت بنت البنت وأطلق في ولد الأم فشمل الذكر والأنثى، وذكر الشارح أن بعد ولد الأم ولده. وأفاده المصنف رحمه الله بتقديم الأم على الأخت تضعيف ما نقله في المستصفى عن شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده رحمه الله، ونقله في التجنيس عن عمر النسفي رحمه الله من أن الأخت الشقيقة أولى من الأم لأنها من قبل الأب، ووجه ضعفه أن الأم أقرب منها . وصرح في الخلاصة بأنه يفتي بتقديم الأم على الأخت، وسيأتي في آخر المختصر أن ذا الرحم قريب ليس ولا عصبة وأن ترتيبهم كترتيب العصبات، فتقدم العمات ثم الأخوال ثم الخالات ثم بنات الأعمام ثم بنات العمات كترتيب الإرث وهو قول الأكثر وظاهر كلام المصنف أن الجد الأخت لأنه من ذوي الأرحام، وذكر المصنف في المستصفى أن الجد الفاسد الأخت عند أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف الولاية لهما كما في الميراث. وفي فتح القدير : وقياس ما صح في الجد والأخ من تقدم الجد تقدم الجد الفاسد على الأخت ا هـ. فثبت بهذا أن المذهب أن الجد الفاسد بعد الأم قبل الأخت وفي القنية : أم الأب أولى في التزويج من الأم. وأطلق في نفي العصبة فشمل العصبة النسبية والسببية فمولى العتاقة ثم عصبته على الترتيب السابق يقدمان على الأم، ولم يذكر المصنف مولى الموالاة
After the mother: the daughter, then the granddaughter (son's daughter), then the great-granddaughter (son's son's daughter), then the great-granddaughter (daughter's daughter's daughter). He gave absolute terms regarding the child of the mother, so it includes male and female. The commentator stated that after the child of the mother is his child. The author indicated by prioritizing the mother over the sister the weakness of what was transmitted in al-Mustasfa from Shaykh al-Islam Khwahar Zadeh and in al-Tajnis from Umar al-Nasafi that the full sister is more entitled than the mother because she is from the father's side. The reason for its weakness is that the mother is closer. It is explicitly stated in al-Khulasa that fatwa is given prioritizing the mother over the sister. It will come at the end of al-Mukhtasar that a dhu rahm is a relative but not an asaba, and their order is like the order of asabat, so the paternal aunts are given precedence, then maternal uncles, then maternal aunts, then daughters of paternal uncles, then daughters of paternal aunts, like the order of inheritance. This is the view of the majority. The apparent meaning of the author's statement is that the grandfather [is] the sister because he is from the dhawu al-arham. The author mentioned in al-Mustasfa that the defective grandfather [takes precedence over] the sister according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Abu Yusuf both have guardianship as in inheritance. In Fath al-Qadir: By analogy with what is established regarding the grandfather and brother of the grandfather's precedence, the defective grandfather takes precedence over the sister. So it is established that the madhhab is that the defective grandfather is after the mother before the sister. In al-Qunyah: The father's mother is more entitled to marriage than the mother. He gave absolute terms regarding the negation of asaba, so it includes relative and cause-based asaba. So the master of emancipation (mawla al-'itaqa) then his asabat in the previous order are given precedence over the mother. The author did not mention the mawla al-muwalah.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes the order of marriage guardians (awliya') after the father. It begins by listing the sequence: after the mother comes the daughter, then the son's daughter, then the son's son's daughter, then the daughter's daughter's daughter. This order is based on proximity of blood relation. The author then addresses a dispute: some early scholars (Khwahar Zadeh and Umar al-Nasafi) held that the full sister (al-ukht al-shaqiqa) is given precedence over the mother because she is from the father's side, but the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq sides with the majority view that the mother is closer and thus takes precedence. He cites al-Khulasa that fatwa is given on this. The passage then discusses the order of asabat (agnatic relatives) and dhawu al-arham (uterine relatives). It mentions that the defective grandfather (al-jadd al-fasid) is preferred over the sister according to Abu Hanifa, while Abu Yusuf gives them equal authority as in inheritance. The relied-upon position (madhhab) is that the defective grandfather comes after the mother and before the sister. A note from al-Qunyah says that the father's mother (grandmother) is more entitled than the mother in marriage. The passage also clarifies that the master of emancipation (mawla al-'itaqa) and his asabat take precedence over the mother. Overall, the lesson is a detailed enumeration of the hierarchy, emphasizing the importance of proximity and legal categories.

Key Terms
ذو الرحم (dhu al-rahm): A relative who is not an asaba (agnate) nor a Quranic sharer; may inherit in some cases.
الجد الفاسد (al-jadd al-fasid): A grandfather who is not a true agnate (e.g., maternal grandfather), considered a dhu rahm.
العصبة (al-asaba): Agnatic relatives who inherit by residuary (asabah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), who takes precedence in marriage guardianship between the mother and the full sister?
A) The full sister, because she is from the father's side.
B) The mother, because she is closer in relation.
C) They are equal and both can marry the woman without priority.
D) The father's mother (grandmother) takes precedence over both.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi marriage guardianship, proximity of blood relation determines precedence; the mother outranks the sister, and the defective grandfather comes after the mother but before the sister in the relied-upon position.

Nikah — Marriage

Order of Non-Agnatic Guardians and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on the order of non-agnatic guardians and the related intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of non-agnatic marriage guardians and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his companions on the basis of walayah.

Core Idea
Non-agnatic relatives have marriage guardianship in a specific order, starting with the mother, after the agnates.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on who may give a woman in marriage when no agnatic guardian (asaba) is available. The matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists the order: mother, sister, then other non-agnatic relatives. However, a major intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf exists: Abu Hanifa holds that all relatives, including non-agnates, have guardianship, while his two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) restrict it to agnates, leaving the judge as the sole guardian. We will unpack the evidence and the resulting practical differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling from Kanz
State the order of non-agnatic guardians after the agnates as given in the matn: mother, then full sister, then half-sister from father, then child of the mother (uterine sibling), then other dhawi al-arham, then the judge.
This order is the mufta bihi (relied-upon position) according to al-Khulasa.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the principle
Note that Abu Hanifa holds that non-agnates have walayah, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that only agnates can be guardians; after agnates, the judge alone is the guardian.
This ikhtilaf affects the entire order: if only agnates have walayah, the list of non-agnates becomes irrelevant.
3
Examine the dalil for Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa's proof: Guardianship is based on consideration (nazar) and kinship prompts compassion; non-agnates also possess this compassion. The hadith 'al-nikahu ila al-asabat' is interpreted as indicating an order of priority, not exclusivity.
The Hanafi usul principle: the absolute (mutlaq) can be restricted (muqayyad) by the reason (illa) of compassion.
4
Examine the Sahibayn's dalil and the Hanafi response
The Sahibayn cite the same hadith as proof of exclusivity. The Hanafi response: the hadith is about order; the illa (compassion) is not confined to agnates. The passage also notes a difference of opinion on Abu Yusuf's final stance, with most sources placing him with Abu Hanifa.
The text mentions conflicting narratives in al-Hidaya, al-Kafi, etc., but the relied-upon view is that the Sahibayn differ.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the thamarah al-khilaf
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, as recorded in Kanz and supported by later texts like al-Khulasa. The practical consequence: if no agnates, a non-agnatic relative (e.g., mother) can marry the woman, whereas according to the Sahibayn, only the judge can perform the marriage.
This difference has direct implications for the validity of marriage contracts in the absence of agnates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بذي سهم . بعد الأم البنت لأنه خاص بالمجنون والمجنونة فبعد الأم البنت ثم بنت الابن ثم بنت ابن الابن ثم بنت بنت البنت وأطلق في ولد الأم فشمل الذكر والأنثى، وذكر الشارح أن بعد ولد الأم ولده. وأفاده المصنف رحمه الله بتقديم الأم على الأخت تضعيف ما نقله في المستصفى عن شيخ الإسلام خواهر زاده رحمه الله، ونقله في التجنيس عن عمر النسفي رحمه الله من أن الأخت الشقيقة أولى من الأم لأنها من قبل الأب، ووجه ضعفه أن الأم أقرب منها . وصرح في الخلاصة بأنه يفتي بتقديم الأم على الأخت، وسيأتي في آخر المختصر أن ذا الرحم قريب ليس ولا عصبة وأن ترتيبهم كترتيب العصبات، فتقدم العمات ثم الأخوال ثم الخالات ثم بنات الأعمام ثم بنات العمات كترتيب الإرث وهو قول الأكثر وظاهر كلام المصنف أن الجد الأخت لأنه من ذوي الأرحام، وذكر المصنف في المستصفى أن الجد الفاسد الأخت عند أبي حنيفة وعند أبي يوسف الولاية لهما كما في الميراث. وفي فتح القدير : وقياس ما صح في الجد والأخ من تقدم الجد تقدم الجد الفاسد على الأخت ا هـ. فثبت بهذا أن المذهب أن الجد الفاسد بعد الأم قبل الأخت وفي القنية : أم الأب أولى في التزويج من الأم. وأطلق في نفي العصبة فشمل العصبة النسبية والسببية فمولى العتاقة ثم عصبته على الترتيب السابق يقدمان على الأم، ولم يذكر المصنف مولى الموالاة وهو الذي أسلم أبو الصغير على يديه ووالاه قالوا : إن آخر الأولياء مقدم على القاضي لأن هذا العقد يفيد الخلافة في الإرث فيفيد في الإنكاح كالعصبات . الفاسد مؤخر عن وأطلق في الحاكم فشمل الإمام والقاضي لكن قالوا: إن القاضي إنما يملك ذلك إذا كان ذلك في عهده ومنشوره ، فإن لم يكن ذلك في عهده لم يكن ولياً. كذا في الظهيرية وغيرها. وفي المجتبى ما يفيد أن لنائب القاضي ولاية التزويج حيث كان القاضي كتب له في هي يقتضي أن الجدة التي لأم فتلي الأم. وقد يقال : إن الجدة التي لأم والجدة التي لأب رتبتهما واحدة فتثبت ولاية التزويج لهما في رتبة واحدة لعدم المرجح من أقربية واحدة. وقد يقال : إن قرابة الأب لها حكم العصبة فتقدم أم الأب على أم الأم فليتأمل اهـ . قلت : وهذا الذي جزم به الرملي كما سيأتي قوله : (ثم بنت بنت البنت قال الرملي : ثم أم الأب ثم أم الأم ثم الجد الفاسد وعليك أن تتأمل في هذا وفيما يأتي قوله: (وفي القنية أم الأب أولى الخ) قال الرملي قال في النهر : هذا الترتيب يعني ترتيب الكنز هو المفتى به كما في الخلاصة وحكى عن خواهر زاده وعمر النسفي تقديم الأخت على الأم لأنها من قوم الأب أقول : وينبغي أن يخرج ما في القنية على هذا القول ا هـ. فقد علمت به ضعف ما في القنية لأنه مقابل لما عليه الفتوى وقيد فيها بالأم لأن الجدة لأب أولى من الجدة لأم قولاً واحدةً فتحصل بعد فتحصل بعد الأم أم الأب ثم أم لأم ثم الجد الفاسد تأمل . ا هـ كلام الرملي قوله : (وفي المجتبي ما يفيد الخ قال في النهر : إن ما في المجتبي لا يفيد عدم اشتراط للأم ثم للأخت لأب وأم ثم لأب ثم لولد الأم ثم لذوي الأرحام ثم للحاكم وللأبعد ويجري بينهما التوارث وكما لا تثبت الولاية لكافر على مسلم كذلك لا تثبت لمسلم على كافرة أعني ولاية التزويج بالقرابة وولاية التصرف في المال قالوا: وينبغي أن يقال إلا أن يكون المسلم سيد أمة كافرة أو سلطاناً . قال :السروجي: لم أر هذا الاستثناء في كتب أصحابنا وإنما هو منسوب إلى الشافعي ومالك . قال في المعراج : وينبغي أن يكون مراداً ورأيت في موضع معزواً إلى المبسوط : الولاية بالسبب العام تثبت للمسلم على الكافر كولاية السلطنة والشهادة فقد ذكر معنى ذلك الاستثناء ا.هـ. وقيد بالكفر لأن الفسق لا يسلب الأهلية عندنا على المشهور وهو المذكور في المنظومة، وعن الشافعي اختلاف فيه أما المستور فله الولاية بلا خلاف، فما في الجوامع أن الأب إذا كان فاسقاً للقاضي أن يزوج الصغيرة من كفء غير معروف. نعم إذا كان متهتكاً لا ينفذ تزويجه إياها بنقص عن مهر المثل ومن غير كفء وسيأتي هذا. كذا في فتح القدير . قوله : ( وإن لم يكن عصبة فالولاية للأم ثم للأخت لأب وأم ثم لأب ثم لولد الأم ثم لذوي الأرحام ثم للحاكم وهذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعندهما ليس لغير العصبات الأقارب ولاية وإنما الولاية للحاكم بعد العصبات لحديث الإنكاح إلى العصبات، ولأبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه أن الولاية نظرية والنظر يتحقق بالتفويض إلى من هو المختص بالقرابة الباعثة على الشفقة. وقد اختلفوا في قول أبي يوسف؛ ففي الهداية الأشهر أنه مع وفي الكافي الجمهور أنه مع أبي حنيفة، وفي التبيين والجوهرة والمجتبى والذخيرة الأصح أنه مع أبي حنيفة، وفي تهذيب القلانسي وروى ابن زياد عن أبي حنيفة وهو قولهما لا يليه إلا العصبات وعليه الفتوى ا هـ . وهو غريب لمخالفته المتون الموضوعة لبيان الفتوى، ولم يذكر قول المصنف : فالولاية) (للام قال الرملي : لم يذكر أم الأم. وفي الجوهرة: وأولاهم الأم ثم الجدة ثم الأخت لأب وأم إلى آخر ما ذكره وفي شرح المجمع لابن الملك: والأم وأقاربها كالجدة والخال والخالة ومثله في شرح المصنف ا.هـ. أقول : لا يظهر من عبارة المجمع مرتبة الجدة في أنها مقدمة على الأخت كما هو صريح عبارة الجوهرة، وقد أغفل في كثير من الكتب المعتبرة ذكر الجدة، بذكرها وبتقديمها على الأخت كما هو الجوهرة العلامة قاسم في شرح النقاية نقله عنه الشرنبلالي في رسالة له خاصة وقال : ولم يقيد الجدة بكونها لأم أو لأب غير أن السياق يقتضي أنها الجدة لأم، وعلى ذلك لا يعلم حكم الجدة لأب هل تقدم على الجدة لأم أو تتأخر عنها أو تزاحمها في ولاية التزويج . ثم نقل الشرنبلالي ما يأتي عن القنية من أن أم الأب أولى من الأم وقال : فعلى هذا تكون أم الأب متقدمة على أم الأم لتقدمها على الأم، لكن المتون تقتضي خلاف ما في القنية، ففي الكنز جعل الأم تلي العصبة فيقدم ما في المتون، وقد يقال : حيث ذكر في القنية تقديم أم الأب على الأم وعارضه الكنز كانت أم الأب تلي الأم بطريق الدلالة لكن يعارضه سياق الشيخ قاسم الذي
With a share... After the mother, the daughter because it is specific to the insane male and female, so after the mother the daughter, then the son's daughter, then the son's son's daughter, then the daughter's daughter's daughter. And he was absolute in the child of the mother, so it includes male and female. And the commentator mentioned that after the child of the mother, his child. And the author, may Allah have mercy on him, indicated by giving precedence to the mother over the sister a weakening of what he transmitted in al-Mustasfa from Shaykh al-Islam Kharzada, may Allah have mercy on him, and transmitted in al-Tajnisa from Umar al-Nasafi, may Allah have mercy on him, that the full sister is more entitled than the mother because she is from the father's side, and the weakness of that is that the mother is closer to her. And it is explicitly stated in al-Khulasa that he gives fatwa giving precedence to the mother over the sister. And it will come at the end of al-Mukhtasar that the dhu rahm is a relative, not an asaba, and their order is like the order of the asabat, so the paternal aunts take precedence, then the maternal uncles, then the maternal aunts, then the daughters of paternal uncles, then the daughters of paternal aunts, like the order of inheritance, and that is the saying of the majority, and the apparent meaning of the author's words is that the grandfather [is] the sister because he is among the dhawi al-arham. And the author mentioned in al-Mustasfa that the false grandfather (grandfather through a female) [is] the sister according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Abu Yusuf, the marriage guardianship is for both of them as in inheritance. And in Fath al-Qadir: By analogy with what is established regarding the grandfather and brother of the grandfather's precedence, the false grandfather takes precedence over the sister. So it is established by this that the madhhab is that the false grandfather is after the mother and before the sister. And in al-Quniya: The father's mother is more entitled to marriage than the mother. And he was absolute in negating the asaba, so it includes asaba by lineage and by cause; thus the freed slave (mawla al-itaqa) then his asaba in the previous order take precedence over the mother. And the author did not mention the mawla al-muwalah, who is the one on whose hands the father of the minor embraced Islam and he became his mawla. They said: The last of the guardians is given precedence over the judge because this contract entails succession in inheritance, so it entails marriage like the asabat. The false [grandfather] is delayed from... And he was absolute in the ruler, so it includes the imam and the judge, but they said: The judge only has that if it is in his term and jurisdiction; if it is not in his term, he is not a guardian. Thus in al-Zahiriyya and others. And in al-Mujtaba, what indicates that the deputy of the judge has the authority of marriage if the judge wrote to him... It requires that the grandmother from the mother follows the mother. And it may be said: The grandmother from the mother and the grandmother from the father are of the same rank, so the marriage guardianship is established for them in the same rank due to no preference of one being closer. And it may be said: The father's kinship has the ruling of asaba, so the father's mother is given precedence over the mother's mother, so consider it... I said: This is what al-Ramli decided, as will come in his saying: (Then the daughter's daughter's daughter). Al-Ramli said: Then the father's mother, then the mother's mother, then the false grandfather. And you must consider this and what follows. His saying: (And in al-Quniya: The father's mother is more entitled etc.) Al-Ramli said in al-Nahr: This order, meaning the order of al-Kanz, is the one given fatwa with, as in al-Khulasa. And it is narrated from Kharzada and Umar al-Nasafi giving precedence to the sister over the mother because she is from the father's people. I say: And it should be that what is in al-Quniya is excluded on this saying. So you know the weakness of what is in al-Quniya because it is opposite to that on which fatwa is based. And it is restricted with the mother because the father's grandmother is more entitled than the mother's grandmother by one saying. So after the mother, the father's mother then the mother's mother then the false grandfather. Consider the end of al-Ramli's speech. His saying: (And in al-Mujtaba what indicates etc.) He said in al-Nahr: What is in al-Mujtaba does not indicate the lack of condition... For the mother then for the full sister then for the half sister from father then for the sister from father then for the child of the mother then for the dhawi al-arham then for the judge and for the more distant. And inheritance occurs between them. And just as guardianship is not established for a disbeliever over a Muslim, likewise it is not established for a Muslim over a disbeliever, meaning marriage guardianship by kinship and guardianship of disposal of property. They said: It should be said except if the Muslim is the master of a disbelieving slave-girl or a sultan. Al-Saruji said: I have not seen this exception in the books of our companions; rather it is attributed to al-Shafi'i and Malik. Al-Maraj said: It should be intended, and I saw in a place attributed to al-Mabsut: Guardianship by general cause is established for a Muslim over a disbeliever, like guardianship of sovereignty and testimony. So the meaning of that exception was mentioned. And it is restricted by disbelief because sinfulness does not remove eligibility according to us, as is well-known and mentioned in al-Manẓuma. And from al-Shafi'i there is a difference of opinion. As for the one whose condition is concealed, he has guardianship without dispute. So what is in al-Jawami' that if the father is sinful, the judge may marry the minor girl to a suitable match not known. Yes, if he is reckless, his marriage of her with a deficiency from the dower of the like and from a non-suitable match will not be executed, and this will come later. Thus in Fath al-Qadir. His saying: (And if there is no asaba, then guardianship is for the mother, then for the full sister, then for the half sister from father, then for the child of the mother, then for the dhawi al-arham, then for the judge). This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And according to the two companions, there is no guardianship for non-asaba relatives, and guardianship is only for the judge after the asaba, based on the hadith: Marriage is for the asaba. And for Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, guardianship is based on consideration (nazar), and consideration is realized by entrusting it to the one who is specifically connected by kinship that prompts compassion. And they differed regarding Abu Yusuf's statement: In al-Hidaya, the most famous is that he is with Muhammad; in al-Kafi, the majority is that he is with Abu Hanifa; in al-Tabyin, al-Jawhara, al-Mujtaba, and al-Dhakhira, the soundest is that he is with Abu Hanifa; and in Tahdhib al-Qalanisi, Ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa, and it is the statement of the two companions that none but the asaba have guardianship, and fatwa is given upon it. This is strange because it contradicts the texts set up to state the fatwa, and he did not mention the author's saying: (The guardianship is for the mother). Al-Ramli said: He did not mention the mother's mother. And in al-Jawhara: The first of them is the mother, then the grandmother, then the full sister, to the end of what he mentioned. And in Sharh al-Majma' by Ibn al-Malik: The mother and her relatives like the grandmother, maternal uncle, and maternal aunt. And similarly in the author's commentary. I say: It is not apparent from the wording of al-Majma' the rank of the grandmother that she is given precedence over the sister, as is explicit in the wording of al-Jawhara. And many reliable books have neglected mentioning the grandmother. The scholar Qasim in Sharh al-Nuqaya mentioned her and gave her precedence over the sister, as in al-Jawhara. Al-Shurnubalali transmitted it from him in a special treatise and said: He did not restrict the grandmother to being from the mother or father, but the context requires that she is the grandmother from the mother, and therefore the ruling for the grandmother from the father is not known: whether she takes precedence over the grandmother from the mother, or is delayed, or shares the same rank in marriage guardianship. Then al-Shurnubalali transmitted what follows from al-Quniya that the father's mother is more entitled than the mother, and said: On this basis, the father's mother takes precedence over the mother's mother because of her precedence over the mother, but the texts contradict what is in al-Quniya. In al-Kanz, he made the mother follow the asaba, so what is in the texts takes precedence. And it may be said: Since al-Quniya mentioned the precedence of the father's mother over the mother and al-Kanz contradicted it, the father's mother follows the mother by indication, but it is contradicted by the context of Shaykh Qasim which...
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding the order of marriage guardians after the agnatic relatives (asabat). The author, Imam al-Marghinani, is expanding on the ruling that if there is no agnatic guardian, then the mother is first, then the sister (full then half), then the children of the mother (uterine siblings), then other dhawi al-arham (non-agnatic relatives), and finally the judge. The author begins by clarifying details: after the mother comes the daughter (specifically for insane individuals), then the son's daughter, etc. He then discusses a dispute: some earlier scholars (e.g., Kharzada and Umar al-Nasafi) held that the full sister is preferred over the mother because she is from the father's side, but the author weakens this view, affirming the mother's precedence due to her greater closeness. The text states that in al-Khulasa, fatwa is given to present the mother. Next, the author addresses the false grandfather (al-jadd al-fasid, i.e., grandfather through a female line) and his rank: according to Abu Hanifa, he is after the mother and before the sister; according to Abu Yusuf, he is equal to the sister. It also mentions the freed slave and his agnates among the guardians, and that the last guardian is presented to the judge. The passage then delves into a major intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that all relatives, even non-agnates, have marriage guardianship (walayah) based on the principle that guardianship is a matter of consideration (nazar) and kinship prompts compassion. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that only agnates have guardianship, citing the hadith 'marriage is for the agnates.' The text then reports conflicting narratives about Abu Yusuf's final position, with most sources stating he agreed with Abu Hanifa, but some saying he sided with Muhammad. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the author is the one in the matn (Kanz) which follows Abu Hanifa. The passage also discusses the grandmother: al-Ramli notes that the Kanz did not mention the grandmother, but al-Jawhara includes her after the mother and before the sister. There is further discussion on whether the paternal grandmother (um al-ab) or maternal grandmother (um al-umm) takes precedence, with some texts (like al-Quniya) stating that the father's mother is preferred over the mother herself, but this is countered by the matn. Finally, the passage addresses the condition of faith in the guardian: a Muslim cannot be guardian over a disbeliever, nor vice versa, with an exception for a Muslim master of a disbelieving slave-girl or the sultan. It also notes that sinfulness (fisq) does not remove eligibility for guardianship, though some scholars disagree. The commentary is rich with citations from earlier Hanafi sources, illustrating the depth of legal reasoning and the process of tarjih (preference) within the school.

Key Terms
العصبة (al-asabah): Agnatic relatives (male line) who inherit as residuaries and have marriage guardianship.
ذو الرحم (dhu al-rahm): Blood relative who is not an asaba; non-agnatic relative (e.g., mother, sister, grandmother, maternal uncle).
الولي (al-wali): The guardian responsible for contracting marriage; can be agnatic, non-agnatic, or the judge.
الجد الفاسد (al-jadd al-fasid): False grandfather: a male ancestor through a female link (e.g., mother's father).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position, who is the first non-agnatic guardian after the agnates?
A) The full sister
B) The judge
C) The mother
D) The grandmother

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school, following Abu Hanifa, includes non-agnatic relatives as marriage guardians, with a specific order beginning with the mother, while the Sahibayn restrict to agnates only; the mufta bihi position follows Abu Hanifa.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Disqualifications for Marriage Guardianship (Wilayah)
Ruling with proof on disqualifications and exceptions for marriage guardianship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the categories of persons disqualified from acting as marriage guardians in Hanafi fiqh, identify the Quranic proof, and explain the exception for a Muslim master or sultan.

Core Idea
A marriage guardian must have full legal capacity; slaves, minors, the insane, and non-Muslims over Muslims lack this.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains who cannot serve as a marriage guardian (wali) in Hanafi law. The rules derive from the principle that guardianship requires both legal capacity and the ability to act in the ward's best interest. The text covers disqualifications due to lack of capacity (minority, slavery, insanity) and due to difference in religion (non-Muslim over Muslim), along with a notable exception regarding Muslim masters and rulers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disqualifications
The text lists four types: minor child, slave, insane person, and non-Muslim over a Muslim. Note the common thread: each lacks full legal capacity over themselves.
The disqualifications are based on the principle that one cannot be a guardian over others if they lack control over themselves.
2
Examine the proof for non-Muslim over Muslim
The Quranic verse 4:141 is cited: 'And Allah will never grant the disbelievers a way over the believers.' Explain that this 'way' (sabil) includes guardianship. Also, verse 8:73 shows mutual guardianship among disbelievers.
The proof is qat'i in thubut and dalala.
3
Analyze the exception
The text mentions an exception for a Muslim master over his disbelieving slave-girl and for a sultan over disbelievers. Note that this exception is not universally accepted in Hanafi works; it is attributed to al-Shafi'i and Malik.
Al-Siruji did not find this exception in Hanafi texts, but al-Mabsut supports it for general cause guardianship.
4
Distinguish between continuous and non-continuous insanity
Only the continuously insane (muṭbiq) loses guardianship. For one with lucid intervals, guardianship is suspended during insanity but resumes during lucidity.
The text clarifies that the insane person in the ruling is the muṭbiq, and the fatwa is upon that.
5
Apply the ruling on fisq
Sinfulness (fisq) does not remove guardianship eligibility in the Hanafi school. However, if the guardian is reckless (mutahattik) and marries the ward to a non-suitable match or for less than the proper mahr, that marriage may be invalidated.
This is a key difference from some Shafi'i views.

Source Text

وكما لا تثبت الولاية لكافر على مسلم كذلك لا تثبت لمسلم على كافرة أعني ولاية التزويج بالقرابة وولاية التصرف في المال قالوا: وينبغي أن يقال إلا أن يكون المسلم سيد أمة كافرة أو سلطاناً . قال :السروجي: لم أر هذا الاستثناء في كتب أصحابنا وإنما هو منسوب إلى الشافعي ومالك . قال في المعراج : وينبغي أن يكون مراداً ورأيت في موضع معزواً إلى المبسوط : الولاية بالسبب العام تثبت للمسلم على الكافر كولاية السلطنة والشهادة فقد ذكر معنى ذلك الاستثناء ا.هـ. وقيد بالكفر لأن الفسق لا يسلب الأهلية عندنا على المشهور وهو المذكور في المنظومة، وعن الشافعي اختلاف فيه أما المستور فله الولاية بلا خلاف، فما في الجوامع أن الأب إذا كان فاسقاً للقاضي أن يزوج الصغيرة من كفء غير معروف. نعم إذا كان متهتكاً لا ينفذ تزويجه إياها بنقص عن مهر المثل ومن غير كفء وسيأتي من هذا. كذا في فتح القدير . قوله : (ولا ولاية لصغير وعبد ومجنون) لأنه لا ولاية لهم على أنفسهم فأولى أن لا يثبت على غيرهم، ولأن هذه ولاية نظرية ولا نظر في التفويض إلى هؤلاء أطلق في العبد فشمل المكاتب فلا ولاية له على ولده كذا في المحيط. لكن للمكاتب ولاية في تزويج أمته كما عرف وأراد بالمجنون المطبق وهو شهر يحتاج إلى تقييده به وعليه الفتوى. وفي فتح القدير : لأنه لا حال جنونه مطبقاً أو يزوج حالة إفاقته عن جنون مطبق أو غير مطبق، لكن المعنى أنه إذا كان مطبقاً غير مطبق، ويزوج تسلب ولايته فتزوج ولا ينتظر إفاقته، وغير المطبق الولاية ثابتة له فلا تزوج وتنتظر إفاقته كالنائم. ومقتضى النظر أن الكفء الخاطب إن فات بانتظار إفاقته تزوج وإن لم يكن مطبقاً وإلا انتظر على ما اختاره المتأخرون في غيبة الولي الأقرب ا هـ قوله : (ولا لكافر على مسلم) لقوله تعالى ﴿ ولن يجعل الله للكافرين على المؤمنين سبيلاً ﴾ [النساء : ١٤١] ولهذا لا تقبل شهادته عليه ولا يتوارثان قيد بالمسلم لأن للكافر ولاية على ولده الكافر لقوله تعالى ﴿ والذين كفروا بعضهم أولياء بعض ﴾ [الأنفال: ۷۳] ولهذا تقبل شهادتهم على بعضهم
And just as guardianship is not established for a disbeliever over a Muslim, likewise it is not established for a Muslim over a disbelieving woman, meaning the guardianship of marriage through kinship and the guardianship of disposal over property. They said: It should be said except if the Muslim is the master of a disbelieving slave-girl or a sultan. Al-Siruji said: I did not see this exception in the books of our companions; rather it is attributed to al-Shafi'i and Malik. Al-Mi'raj said: It should be intended, and I saw in a place attributed to al-Mabsut: Guardianship by general cause is established for the Muslim over the disbeliever, like the guardianship of sovereignty and testimony, thus the meaning of that exception was mentioned. End. And it was restricted to disbelief because transgression (fisq) does not remove eligibility according to us according to the well-known view, and it is mentioned in al-Manẓūma. From al-Shafi'i there is a difference of opinion. As for the one who is concealed (mastūr), he has guardianship without dispute. What is in al-Jawāmi‘ that if the father is a transgressor, the judge may marry off the young girl to a suitable match who is not known. Yes, if he is reckless, his marriage of her is not executed if it is for less than the proper dowry or other than a suitable match, and this will come. Thus in Fatḥ al-Qadīr. His statement: (And no guardianship for a small child, slave, and insane) because they have no guardianship over themselves, so it is more appropriate that it not be established over others, and because this guardianship is a guardianship of consideration, and there is no consideration in delegating to these. He made it absolute regarding the slave, so it includes the mukātab, so he has no guardianship over his child, thus in al-Muḥīt. But the mukātab has guardianship in marrying off his slave-girl as is known. And by insane he intended the continuous (muṭbiq) which is a month requires restriction, and upon it is the fatwa. And in Fatḥ al-Qadīr: Because in the state of his insanity, whether continuous or he marries in a state of lucidity after continuous or non-continuous insanity, but the meaning is that if he is continuous, his guardianship is removed, so she marries and his lucidity is not waited for. And the non-continuous has guardianship established, so she does not marry and his lucidity is waited for, like the sleeping. And the requirement of consideration is that if the suitable suitor is lost by waiting for his lucidity, she marries even if not continuous, otherwise she waits according to what the later scholars chose in the absence of the nearest guardian. End. His statement: (And not for a disbeliever over a Muslim) due to His statement the Exalted: 'And Allah will never grant the disbelievers a way over the believers' [4:141]. And for this his testimony is not accepted over him, and they do not inherit from each other. He restricted by Muslim because the disbeliever has guardianship over his disbelieving child due to His statement the Exalted: 'And those who disbelieve are allies of one another' [8:73]. And for this their testimonies are accepted over each other.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq presents the ruling on who is disqualified from acting as a marriage guardian (wali) in Hanafi fiqh. The author explains that a minor child, a slave, and an insane person are disqualified because they lack full legal capacity over themselves. A minor has no rights over his own affairs, a slave is himself owned, and an insane person lacks reasoning. The commentator clarifies that the 'insane person' here refers specifically to the continuously insane (muṭbiq) who never has lucid intervals; if he has lucid intervals, his guardianship is only suspended during insanity. The same applies to a disbeliever over a Muslim — no guardianship is possible because Allah has declared that disbelievers have no way over believers. The text cites the Quranic verse (4:141) and draws analogy to other rulings like the inadmissibility of a disbeliever's testimony over a Muslim and lack of inheritance. However, an exception is noted: a Muslim master may have guardianship over his disbelieving slave-girl, and a Muslim sultan (ruler) may have general authority over disbelievers. This exception is attributed to al-Shafi'i and Malik, but the Hanafi commentator al-Siruji did not find it in Hanafi texts. Nonetheless, al-Mabsut supports it under 'general cause' guardianship (like sovereign authority or judicial testimony). Additionally, the text discusses that fisq (sinfulness) does not strip guardianship eligibility in the Hanafi school, unlike the Shafi'i school where there is difference. A fasiq father still has the right to marry off his minor daughter, but if he is reckless (mutahattik) and marries her for less than the proper dowry or to a non-suitable match, that marriage may be invalidated.

Key Terms
ولاية (wilāya): Guardianship, specifically the authority to contract marriage on behalf of someone who lacks capacity (e.g., minor, insane).
مجنون مطبق (majnūn muṭbiq): A continuously insane person who never has lucid intervals.
فسق (fisq): Sinfulness, transgression; here refers to a person who commits major sins but is not necessarily an open sinner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of insane person loses the right of guardianship in marriage?
A) The one who is insane continuously (muṭbiq)
B) The one who has lucid intervals
C) Both A and B
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
A marriage guardian must be Muslim (if ward is Muslim), adult, free, and sane; exceptions exist for Muslim masters and sultans, but are disputed within the school.

Guardianship After Agnates: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on guardianship order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on guardianship when no agnates exist and explain the legal reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
A woman with no agnates: Abu Hanifa empowers close relatives; Sahibayn reserve to the judge.

The dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two companions on guardianship after agnates is a classic intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. This lesson unpacks the two views, the hadith evidence, and the principle of wilāya naẓariyya that underlies Abu Hanifa's extension of guardianship to non-agnate relatives.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Read the passage and determine the precise point of disagreement: after the agnates (ʿaṣaba) are exhausted, who may act as marriage guardian?
Abu Hanifa names a sequence; the Sahibayn stop at the judge.
2
Examine the dalīl of the Sahibayn
Locate the hadith cited: 'al-inkāh ilā al-ʿaṣabāt'. Understand its apparent implication – only agnates have guardianship.
This is a dalīl naqlī (textual proof).
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's counter-dalīl
Abu Hanifa argues that guardianship is 'naẓariyya' (based on consideration) and that close relatives, even if not agnates, possess the required compassion (shafaqa) and can assess the woman's interest.
This is a taʿlīl (ratio-based reasoning) that broadens the scope.
4
Note the dispute over Abu Yusuf's stance
The passage shows conflicting reports on whether Abu Yusuf agreed with Abu Hanifa or with Muhammad al-Shaybānī. Understand that such intra-Hanafi differences affect the weight of the transmitted positions.
Later fatwā is often on the side of the Sahibayn, but many authoritative texts prefer Abu Hanifa.
5
Apply the dispute to a scenario
Consider a woman with no agnates: under each view, who marries her off? Abu Hanifa: mother (then sister, etc.); Sahibayn: only the judge. This is the thamarah al-khilāf.
The practical difference determines the validity of the marriage contract.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وإن لم يكن عصبة فالولاية للأم ثم للأخت لأب وأم ثم لأب ثم لولد الأم ثم لذوي الأرحام ثم للحاكم وهذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى، وعندهما ليس لغير العصبات الأقارب ولاية وإنما الولاية للحاكم بعد العصبات لحديث الإنكاح إلى العصبات، ولأبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه أن الولاية نظرية والنظر يتحقق بالتفويض إلى من هو المختص بالقرابة الباعثة على الشفقة. وقد اختلفوا في قول أبي يوسف؛ ففي الهداية الأشهر أنه مع وفي الكافي الجمهور أنه مع أبي حنيفة، وفي التبيين والجوهرة والمجتبى والذخيرة الأصح أنه مع أبي حنيفة، وفي تهذيب القلانسي وروى ابن زياد عن أبي حنيفة وهو قولهما لا يليه إلا العصبات وعليه الفتوى ا هـ . وهو غريب لمخالفته المتون الموضوعة لبيان الفتوى، ولم يذكر وممن صرح محمد، قول المصنف : فالولاية) (للام قال الرملي : لم يذكر أم الأم. وفي الجوهرة: وأولاهم الأم ثم الجدة ثم الأخت لأب وأم إلى آخر ما ذكره وفي شرح المجمع لابن الملك: والأم وأقاربها كالجدة والخال والخالة ومثله في شرح المصنف ا.هـ. أقول : لا يظهر من عبارة المجمع مرتبة الجدة في أنها مقدمة على الأخت كما هو صريح عبارة الجوهرة، وقد أغفل في كثير من الكتب المعتبرة ذكر الجدة، بذكرها وبتقديمها على الأخت كما هو الجوهرة العلامة قاسم في شرح النقاية نقله عنه الشرنبلالي في رسالة له خاصة وقال : ولم يقيد الجدة بكونها لأم أو لأب غير أن السياق يقتضي أنها الجدة لأم، وعلى ذلك لا يعلم حكم الجدة لأب هل تقدم على الجدة لأم أو تتأخر عنها أو تزاحمها في ولاية التزويج . ثم نقل الشرنبلالي ما يأتي عن القنية من أن أم الأب أولى من الأم وقال : فعلى هذا تكون أم الأب متقدمة على أم الأم لتقدمها على الأم، لكن المتون تقتضي خلاف ما في القنية، ففي الكنز جعل الأم تلي العصبة فيقدم ما في المتون، وقد يقال : حيث ذكر في القنية تقديم أم الأب على الأم وعارضه الكنز كانت أم الأب تلي الأم بطريق الدلالة لكن يعارضه سياق الشيخ قاسم الذي
His statement: (And if there is no agnate, then guardianship belongs to the mother, then to the full or consanguine sister, then to the paternal aunt, then to the uterine brother's child, then to the kindred (dhawu al-arham), then to the judge. And this is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And according to the two companions, there is no guardianship for relatives other than agnates; rather, guardianship goes to the judge after the agnates, due to the hadith 'Marriage belongs to the agnates.' And for Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, that guardianship is a matter of consideration (nazariyya), and consideration is realized by delegating to the one who is specially connected by kinship that motivates compassion. And they differed regarding the opinion of Abu Yusuf; in al-Hidaya, the more well-known is that he is with [the two companions], and in al-Kafi, the majority is that he is with Abu Hanifa, and in al-Tabyin, al-Jawhara, al-Mujtaba, and al-Dhakhira, the most correct is that he is with Abu Hanifa, and in Tahdhib al-Qalanisi, Ibn Ziyad narrated from Abu Hanifa that it is the opinion of the two companions that only agnates can be guardians and upon it is the fatwa. End. And this is strange because it contradicts the texts (mutun) written to clarify the fatwa, and he did not mention who explicitly stated Muhammad. The author's statement: (Then guardianship) for the mother. Al-Ramli said: He did not mention the maternal grandmother. And in al-Jawhara: The first of them is the mother, then the grandmother, then the full or consanguine sister, etc. as he mentioned. And in Sharh al-Majma‘ by Ibn al-Malik: The mother and her relatives like the grandmother, maternal uncle, and maternal aunt, and similarly in Sharh al-Musannaf. End. I say: It is not apparent from the expression of al-Majma‘ the rank of the grandmother in being preferred over the sister as is explicit in the expression of al-Jawhara, and many reliable books have neglected mentioning the grandmother, mentioning her and preferring her over the sister as in al-Jawhara by ‘Allama Qasim in Sharh al-Niqaya, quoted by al-Shurunbulali in a special treatise of his, and he said: He did not restrict the grandmother to being maternal or paternal, but the context indicates that she is the maternal grandmother. On that, the ruling for the paternal grandmother is not known whether she is preferred over the maternal grandmother, or comes after, or shares equally in guardianship of marriage. Then al-Shurunbulali quoted what follows from al-Qunyah that the paternal grandmother is more entitled than the mother, and said: On this basis, the paternal grandmother is ahead of the maternal grandmother due to her precedence over the mother, but the texts (mutun) imply otherwise than what is in al-Qunyah, for in al-Kanz the mother is placed after the agnate, so what is in the texts is preferred. And it may be said: Since al-Qunyah mentioned the preference of the paternal grandmother over the mother and al-Kanz opposes it, the paternal grandmother comes after the mother by implication, but this is opposed by the context of Shaykh Qasim which...
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents the well-known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two companions, Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the order of marriage guardians when there is no agnate (asaba). According to Abu Hanifa, after the agnates, the right of guardianship passes to the mother, then to the sister (full or consanguine), then to the paternal aunt, then to the children of the maternal uncle, then to other kindred (dhawu al-arham), and finally to the judge. The two companions, however, hold that only agnates can be guardians; if there are no agnates, the right goes directly to the judge. Their proof is the hadith 'al-inkah ila al-asabat' (marriage is for the agnates). Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that guardianship is a matter of consideration (nazariyya), and the most considerate person is the one who is closest in kinship and has natural compassion. The commentator then discusses conflicting reports about Abu Yusuf's position: some sources say he agreed with Abu Hanifa, others that he agreed with Muhammad. The most authoritative view (al-sahh) is that Abu Yusuf sided with Abu Hanifa, but there is a narration that he eventually agreed with Muhammad and the fatwa is on that. However, the author of al-Hidaya finds this strange because it contradicts the established texts (mutun) that are the basis of fatwa. The discussion also extends to the order within Abu Hanifa's list: whether the maternal grandmother is included, whether she is preferred over the sister, and the position of the paternal grandmother. Al-Shurunbulali notes a disagreement: al-Qunyah ranks the paternal grandmother ahead of the mother, while al-Kanz places the mother after the agnates, which implies the mother is before the paternal grandmother. The commentator sides with the texts (mutun) over al-Qunyah.

Key Terms
عصبة (ʻaṣaba): Agnatic relatives: male relatives connected through males, e.g., father, brother, paternal uncle, and their descendants.
ولاية نظرية (wilāya naẓariyya): Guardianship based on consideration and careful choice; the guardian must act in the best interest of the woman.
ذوو الأرحام (dhawu al-arḥām): Kindred relatives: uterine relatives who are not agnates (e.g., maternal uncle, maternal aunt, grandchildren through daughters).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two companions (Sahibayn), who becomes the marriage guardian if there is no agnate relative?
A) The mother
B) The sister
C) The judge
D) The paternal aunt

Key Takeaway
The disagreement on guardianship after agnates is a core intra-Hanafi ikhtilāf: Abu Hanifa extends to close relatives via consideration (naẓariyya), while the Ṣāḥibayn restrict to the judge via the ḥadīth 'al-inkāh ilā al-ʿaṣabāt'.
